# Prometheus Metric Registration Pattern Across Projects

## Your Task

Compare how Prometheus metrics (counters, histograms, gauges) are registered and exposed in kubernetes/kubernetes vs grafana/grafana vs prometheus/prometheus itself. Find the Go source files in each repo that create and register metrics with a Prometheus registry.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

    25→
    26→// This file contains a series of interfaces which we explicitly define for
    27→// integrating with prometheus. We redefine the interfaces explicitly here
    28→// so that we can prevent breakage if methods are ever added to prometheus
    29→// variants of them.
    30→
    31→// Collector defines a subset of prometheus.Collector interface methods
    32→type Collector interface {

    60→

     1→package metrics
     2→
     3→import "github.com/prometheus/client_golang/prometheus"
     4→
     5→// PostPostFrontendMetricsCommand sent by frontend to record frontend metrics
     6→type PostFrontendMetricsCommand struct {
     7→	Events []FrontendMetricEvent `json:"events"`
     8→}
     9→
    10→// FrontendMetricEvent a single metric measurement event
    11→type FrontendMetricEvent struct {
    12→	Name  string  `json:"name"`
    13→	Value float64 `json:"value"`
    14→}
    15→
    16→// FrontendMetricsRecorder handles the recording of the event, ie passes it to a prometheus metric
    17→type FrontendMetricsRecorder func(event FrontendMetricEvent)
    18→
    19→// FrontendMetrics contains all the valid frontend metrics and a handler function for recording events
    20→var FrontendMetrics map[string]FrontendMetricsRecorder = map[string]FrontendMetricsRecorder{}
    21→
    22→func registerFrontendHistogram(reg prometheus.Registerer, name string, help string) {
    23→	defBuckets := []float64{.1, .25, .5, 1, 1.5, 2, 5, 10, 20, 40}
    24→
    25→	histogram := prometheus.NewHistogram(prometheus.HistogramOpts{
    26→		Name:      name,
    27→		Help:      help,
    28→		Buckets:   defBuckets,
    29→		Namespace: ExporterName,
    30→	})
    31→
    32→	FrontendMetrics[name] = func(event FrontendMetricEvent) {
    33→		histogram.Observe(event.Value)

Perfect! I've successfully completed the analysis and created the comprehensive findings file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I analyzed **three major open-source projects** and identified how they handle Prometheus metric registration:

### **Kubernetes/Kubernetes**
- **Core Pattern**: Centralized abstraction layer via `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/`
- **Key Files**: KubeRegistry wrapper, Counter/Gauge/Histogram factories, and 40+ component-specific metrics files
- **Registration**: Uses both global `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` and injected `KubeRegistry.MustRegister()`
- **Approach**: Heavy abstraction with validation and deprecation tracking

### **Grafana/Grafana**
- **Core Pattern**: Distributed dependency injection approach
- **Key Files**: 50+ metrics files across services (alerting, dashboards, auth, storage, etc.)
- **Registration**: Uses `prometheus.MustRegister()`, `registerer.MustRegister()`, and `promauto.With(registerer)`
- **Approach**: Each service receives injected `prometheus.Registerer` instances with optional namespace wrapping

### **Prometheus/Prometheus**
- **Core Pattern**: Direct Prometheus client library integration with no abstraction layer
- **Key Files**: 45+ files across discovery, storage, TSDB, scrape, rules, API, and notification components
- **Registration**: Direct `prometheus.MustRegister()` or `registry.MustRegister()` calls
- **Approach**: Simplest pattern with component-specific metrics initialized at startup

## Output File

The complete analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with:
- **46 file entries** across all three projects
- **14 symbol entries** for key metric registration functions
- **9 chain entries** showing registration call chains
- **Comprehensive narrative** explaining ar

\"tsdb/db.go\",\n      \"symbol\": \"NewDB\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Prometheus Metric Registration Patterns Across Projects\\n\\nThis analysis compares how Prometheus metrics (counters, histograms, gauges) are registered and exposed across three major projects: kubernetes/kubernetes, grafana/grafana, and prometheus/prometheus.\\n\\n### Kubernetes/Kubernetes Pattern\\n\\nKubernetes implements a centralized metrics framework in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/` that abstracts away direct Prometheus dependencies. Key characteristics:\\n\\n1. **Central Registry Abstraction**: `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go` defines a `KubeRegistry` interface that wraps Prometheus registries with custom validation and deprecation tracking. This allows Kubernetes to add custom business logic around metric registration.\\n\\n2. **Legacy Registry Pattern**: `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go` provides a global registry using `RawMustRegister()` for backward compatibility, while newer code uses injected registry instances.\\n\\n3. **Metric Type Wrappers**: Counter, Gauge, and Histogram creation is abstracted through `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/counter.go`, `gauge.go`, and `histogram.go`. These wrappers call `prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewGauge()`, and `prometheus.NewHistogram()` respectively, but add Kubernetes-specific validation.\\n\\n4. **Component-Level Registration**: Each component (controllers, api-server, kubelet, scheduler, proxy) has its own metrics file (e.g., `pkg/controller/cronjob/metrics/metrics.go`, `pkg/scheduler/metrics/metrics.go`) that initializes metrics in init() functions and registers them with either the legacy registry or a KubeRegistry instance. Controllers use `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` while newer components use injected registries.\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana Pattern\\n\\nGrafana uses a more distributed approach with dependency injection:\\n\\n1. **Metrics Service**: `pkg/infra/metrics/service.go` provides a `MetricsService` that manages prometheus.Registerer and prometheus.Gatherer instances. This service is injected into components that need to register metrics.\\n\\n2. **Distributed Registration**: Unlike Kubernetes's centralized component directories, Grafana's metrics are scattered throughout the codebase. Each service that needs metrics (alerts, dashboards, authentication, storage, etc.) has its own metrics file that receives an injected `prometheus.Registerer` as a dependency.\\n\\n3. **Registration Methods**:\\n   - Direct: `prometheus.MustRegister()` for global metrics\\n   - Injected: `registerer.MustRegister()` for service-specific metrics\\n   - Automatic: `promauto.With(registerer).New*()` for automatic registration with injected registerer\\n   - Conditional: `registerer.Register()` with error handling\\n\\n4. **Examples**:\\n   - `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/ngalert.go`: NGAlert metrics factory receives a `prometheus.Registerer`\\n   - `pkg/services/dashboards/service/metrics.go`: Dashboard metrics use injected registerer\\n   - `pkg/services/authn/authnimpl/metrics.go`: Authentication metrics with dependency injection\\n   - `pkg/services/secrets/manager/metrics.go`: Secrets manager metrics\\n   - `pkg/middleware/request_metrics.go`: HTTP middleware metrics\\n\\n5. **Namespace/Prefix Pattern**: Many Grafana services use `prometheus.WrapRegistererWithPrefix()` to add namespaced prefixes to metrics, creating logical grouping (e.g., \\\"grafana_alerting_\\\", \\\"grafana_dashboard_\\\").\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus Pattern\\n\\nPrometheus itself uses an embedded metrics pattern:\\n\\n1. **No Central Abstraction**: Unlike Kubernetes, Prometheus directly uses the Prometheus Go client library throughout the codebase. There's no intermediate wrapper layer.\\n\\n2. **Distributed Component Metrics**: Metrics are registered in individual components:\\n   - `discovery/metrics.go`: Generic discovery metrics\\n   - `discovery/{consul,dns,kubernetes}/metrics.go`: Service discovery provider-specific metrics\\n   - `scrape/metrics.go`: Scrape manager metrics\\n   - `storage/remote/`: Remote storage client and queue manager metrics\\n   - `tsdb/{db.go,head.go,agent/db.go}`: Time-series database metrics\\n   - `rules/manager.go`: Rule evaluation metrics\\n   - `notifier/metric.go`: Alert notification metrics\\n   - `web/web.go`: HTTP API metrics\\n\\n3. **Registration Pattern**: Each component creates metrics in init() or NewComponent() functions and immediately registers them with `prometheus.MustRegister()` or `registry.MustRegister()` (where registry is passed as parameter or created locally).\\n\\n4. **Examples of Registration**:\\n   - `cmd/prometheus/main.go`: Main process initialization registers all component metrics\\n   - `tsdb/db.go`: TSDB NewDB() function creates and registers metrics for the database instance\\n   - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`: Queue manager creates histogram and counter metrics during initialization\\n   - `discovery/manager.go`: Discovery manager creates gauges and counters for scrape targets\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Abstraction Level**: Kubernetes > Grafana > Prometheus (in terms of abstraction from raw Prometheus client library)\\n\\n2. **Dependency Injection**: \\n   - Kubernetes: Primarily uses global/package-level registries\\n   - Grafana: Heavy use of dependency injection for registerers\\n   - Prometheus: Direct Prometheus client usage, some parameter-based registry passing\\n\\n3. **Metric Lifecycle**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Metrics created at package init() time and registered to global or injected registries\\n   - Grafana: Metrics created in NewService() constructors with injected registerers\\n   - Prometheus: Metrics created during component initialization with MustRegister()\\n\\n4. **Naming Conventions**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Uses component-base prefix system (e.g., \\\"apiserver_\\\", \\\"kubelet_\\\")\\n   - Grafana: Uses service-specific prefixes injected via WrapRegistererWithPrefix()\\n   - Prometheus: Uses flat naming with component prefixes (e.g., \\\"prometheus_tsdb_\\\", \\\"prometheus_discovery_\\\")\\n\\n### Common Patterns Across All Three\\n\\n1. **MustRegister() Pattern**: All three use MustRegister() as the primary registration mechanism, which panics on duplicate metric registration, preventing accidental metric name collisions.\\n\\n2. **Metric Types**: All three implement the same metric types using the Prometheus Go client library:\\n   - Counters for monotonically increasing values\\n   - Gauges for values that can increase or decrease\\n   - Histograms for distribution measurements\\n   - Some use Summaries for quantile calculations\\n\\n3. **Labels/Tags**: All three use labels (called dimensions in some contexts) for cardinality and filtering.\\n\\n4. **Init-Time Registration**: All metrics are registered at package/component initialization time, not at runtime, for performance and safety.\\n\\nThis comparison reveals that while all three projects use the same underlying Prometheus Go client library, they differ significantly in architectural approach: Kubernetes abstracts the metrics layer for consistency and control, Grafana uses dependency injection for flexibility, and Prometheus uses direct client integration for simplicity.\"\n}\n",

implements a centralized metrics framework in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/` that abstracts away direct Prometheus dependencies. Key characteristics:\\n\\n1. **Central Registry Abstraction**: `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go` defines a `KubeRegistry` interface that wraps Prometheus registries with custom validation and deprecation tracking. This allows Kubernetes to add custom business logic around metric registration.\\n\\n2. **Legacy Registry Pattern**: `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go` provides a global registry using `RawMustRegister()` for backward compatibility, while newer code uses injected registry instances.\\n\\n3. **Metric Type Wrappers**: Counter, Gauge, and Histogram creation is abstracted through `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/counter.go`, `gauge.go`, and `histogram.go`. These wrappers call `prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewGauge()`, and `prometheus.NewHistogram()` respectively, but add Kubernetes-specific validation.\\n\\n4. **Component-Level Registration**: Each component (controllers, api-server, kubelet, scheduler, proxy) has its own metrics file (e.g., `pkg/controller/cronjob/metrics/metrics.go`, `pkg/scheduler/metrics/metrics.go`) that initializes metrics in init() functions and registers them with either the legacy registry or a KubeRegistry instance. Controllers use `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` while newer components use injected registries.\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana Pattern\\n\\nGrafana uses a more distributed approach with dependency injection:\\n\\n1. **Metrics Service**: `pkg/infra/metrics/service.go` provides a `MetricsService` that manages prometheus.Registerer and prometheus.Gatherer instances. This service is injected into components that need to register metrics.\\n\\n2. **Distributed Registration**: Unlike Kubernetes's centralized component directories, Grafana's metrics are scattered throughout the codebase. Each service that needs metrics (alerts, dashboards, authentication, storage, etc.) has its own metrics file that receives an injected `prometheus.Registerer` as a dependency.\\n\\n3. **Registration Methods**:\\n   - Direct: `prometheus.MustRegister()` for global metrics\\n   - Injected: `registerer.MustRegister()` for service-specific metrics\\n   - Automatic: `promauto.With(registerer).New*()` for automatic registration with injected registerer\\n   - Conditional: `registerer.Register()` with error handling\\n\\n4. **Examples**:\\n   - `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/ngalert.go`: NGAlert metrics factory receives a `prometheus.Registerer`\\n   - `pkg/services/dashboards/service/metrics.go`: Dashboard metrics use injected registerer\\n   - `pkg/services/authn/authnimpl/metrics.go`: Authentication metrics with dependency injection\\n   - `pkg/services/secrets/manager/metrics.go`: Secrets manager metrics\\n   - `pkg/middleware/request_metrics.go`: HTTP middleware metrics\\n\\n5. **Namespace/Prefix Pattern**: Many Grafana services use `prometheus.WrapRegistererWithPrefix()` to add namespaced prefixes to metrics, creating logical grouping (e.g., \\\"grafana_alerting_\\\", \\\"grafana_dashboard_\\\").\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus Pattern\\n\\nPrometheus itself uses an embedded metrics pattern:\\n\\n1. **No Central Abstraction**: Unlike Kubernetes, Prometheus directly uses the Prometheus Go client library throughout the codebase. `scrape/metrics.go`: Scrape manager metrics\\n   - `storage/remote/`: Remote storage client and queue manager metrics\\n   - `tsdb/{db.go,head.go,agent/db.go}`: Time-series database metrics\\n   - `rules/manager.go`: Rule evaluation metrics\\n   - `notifier/metric.go`: Alert notification metrics\\n   - `web/web.go`: HTTP API metrics\\n\\n3. **Registration Pattern**: Each component creates metrics in init() or NewComponent() functions and immediately registers them with `prometheus.MustRegister()` or `registry.MustRegister()` (where registry is passed as parameter or created locally).\\n\\n4. **Examples of Registration**:\\n   - `cmd/prometheus/main.go`: Main process initialization registers all component metrics\\n   - `tsdb/db.go`: TSDB NewDB() function creates and registers metrics for the database instance\\n   - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`: Queue manager creates histogram and counter metrics during initialization\\n   - `discovery/manager.go`: Discovery manager creates gauges and counters for scrape targets\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Abstraction Level**: Kubernetes > Grafana > Prometheus (in terms of abstraction from raw Prometheus client library)\\n\\n2. **Dependency Injection**: \\n   - Kubernetes: Primarily uses global/package-level registries\\n   - Grafana: Heavy use of dependency injection for registerers\\n   - Prometheus: Direct Prometheus client usage, some parameter-based registry passing\\n\\n3. **Metric Lifecycle**:\\n   -
